To implement the requested WhatsApp chatbot with the specified features, we will break down the task into several components. Each component will be responsible for a specific part of the application. Here's a high-level overview of the core classes and functions:

1. **main.py**: The entry point of the application.
   - `main()`: Initializes the application and starts the GUI.

2. **gui.py**: Handles the graphical user interface using a Python GUI framework.
   - `AppGUI`: Class to create and manage the GUI.
   - `create_main_window()`: Sets up the main window layout.
   - `update_dashboard()`: Updates the admin dashboard with current bookings.

3. **whatsapp_api.py**: Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
   - `WhatsAppAPI`: Class to handle sending and receiving messages.
   - `send_message()`: Sends a message via WhatsApp.
   - `receive_message()`: Handles incoming messages.

4. **chatgpt_api.py**: Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
   - `ChatGPTAPI`: Class to manage conversations with ChatGPT.
   - `get_response()`: Retrieves a response from ChatGPT based on user input.

5. **database.py**: Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
   - `DatabaseManager`: Class to handle database connections and queries.
   - `register_customer()`: Registers a new customer in the database.
   - `book_service()`: Books a service for a customer.
   - `get_bookings()`: Retrieves current bookings for the admin dashboard.

6. **notifications.py**: Handles notification features.
   - `NotificationManager`: Class to manage sending notifications.
   - `send_notification()`: Sends a notification to a user.

7. **deployment.py**: Handles deployment on HOSTINGER.
   - `deploy_application()`: Deploys the application to HOSTINGER.

Let's start with the implementation of each file:

### main.py

```python
'''

Main entry point for the WhatsApp chatbot application.

'''

from gui import AppGUI

def main():
    app = AppGUI()
    app.create_main_window()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

### database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

### database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

        '''
        Deploys the application to HOSTINGER using the provided credentials.

'''

import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()

```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()

### notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart

class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password

    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)

            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))

            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")

        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

### database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

### notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart

class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password

    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)

            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))

            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")

        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

To implement the `chatgpt_api.py` file and ensure it integrates properly with the rest of the application, we need to define the methods within the `ChatGPTAPI` class. This class will handle interactions with the OpenAI ChatGPT API. Below is the fully implemented code for `chatgpt_api.py` and any necessary modifications to other files to ensure the application functions as intended.

### chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import openai

class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key

    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys.

        api_key (str): The API key for WhatsApp.
        chatgpt_api_key (str): The API key for OpenAI ChatGPT.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(chatgpt_api_key)

    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        # Code to send a message via WhatsApp API
        pass

    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response

        '''

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

To implement the `whatsapp_api.py` file, we need to complete the methods for sending and receiving messages using the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp. Below is the fully implemented code for `whatsapp_api.py`, along with any necessary adjustments to other files to ensure the complete functionality of the application.

### whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key, chatgpt_api_key, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for WhatsApp.
        chatgpt_api_key (str): The API key for OpenAI ChatGPT.
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(chatgpt_api_key)
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"

    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")

    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()

            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):

 To implement the `whatsapp_api.py` file, we need to complete the methods for sending and receiving messages using the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp. Below is the fully implemented code for `whatsapp_api.py`, along with any necessary adjustments to other files to ensure the complete functionality of the application.

### whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key, chatgpt_api_key, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for WhatsApp.
        chatgpt_api_key (str): The API key for OpenAI ChatGPT.
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(chatgpt_api_key)
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"

    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")

    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

'''

'''
import os
import subprocess
from deployment import DeploymentManager

# Example usage

### database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

### notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart

class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password

    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

    def deploy_application(self):
        '''
        Deploys the application to HOSTINGER using the provided credentials.
        '''
        # Simulate deployment process
        print("Starting deployment to HOSTINGER...")
        # Example: Using subprocess to run deployment commands
        try:
            # This is a placeholder for actual deployment commands
            subprocess.run(["echo", "Deploying application..."], check=True)
            print("Application deployed successfully on HOSTINGER.")
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
            print(f"Deployment failed: {e}")

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key, chatgpt_api_key, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for WhatsApp.
        chatgpt_api_key (str): The API key for OpenAI ChatGPT.
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(chatgpt_api_key)
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"
    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key, chatgpt_api_key, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for WhatsApp.
        chatgpt_api_key (str): The API key for OpenAI ChatGPT.
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(chatgpt_api_key)
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"
    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

'''

import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self, smtp_server, smtp_port, smtp_user, smtp_password):
        self.smtp_server = smtp_server
        self.smtp_port = smtp_port
        self.smtp_user = smtp_user
        self.smtp_password = smtp_password
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import os
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI

class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = os.getenv("WHATSAPP_API_KEY")
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(os.getenv("CHATGPT_API_KEY"))
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"

    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")

    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import os
import openai

class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key

    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3

class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()

    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()

    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()

    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import os
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart

class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.smtp_server = os.getenv("SMTP_SERVER")
        self.smtp_port = os.getenv("SMTP_PORT")
        self.smtp_user = os.getenv("SMTP_USER")
        self.smtp_password = os.getenv("SMTP_PASSWORD")

    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import os
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = os.getenv("WHATSAPP_API_KEY")
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(os.getenv("CHATGPT_API_KEY"))
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"
    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import os
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import os
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.smtp_server = os.getenv("SMTP_SERVER")
        self.smtp_port = os.getenv("SMTP_PORT")
        self.smtp_user = os.getenv("SMTP_USER")
        self.smtp_password = os.getenv("SMTP_PASSWORD")
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

'''
Handles deployment of the application on HOSTINGER.

import subprocess
class DeploymentManager:
    def __init__(self, hostinger_credentials):
        self.hostinger_credentials = hostinger_credentials
    def deploy_application(self):
        '''
        Deploys the application to HOSTINGER using the provided credentials.
        '''
        # Simulate deployment process
        print("Starting deployment to HOSTINGER...")
        # Example: Using subprocess to run deployment commands
        try:
            # This is a placeholder for actual deployment commands
            subprocess.run(["echo", "Deploying application..."], check=True)
            print("Application deployed successfully on HOSTINGER.")
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
            print(f"Deployment failed: {e}")

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import os
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = os.getenv("WHATSAPP_API_KEY")
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(os.getenv("CHATGPT_API_KEY"))
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"
    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import os
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import os
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.smtp_server = os.getenv("SMTP_SERVER")
        self.smtp_port = os.getenv("SMTP_PORT")
        self.smtp_user = os.getenv("SMTP_USER")
        self.smtp_password = os.getenv("SMTP_PASSWORD")
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

            # This is a placeholder for actual deployment commands
            subprocess.run(["echo", "Deploying application..."], check=True)
            print("Application deployed successfully on HOSTINGER.")
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
            print(f"Deployment failed: {e}")

        "password": os.getenv("HOSTINGER_PASSWORD")

whatsapp_api.py
```python
'''
Manages interactions with the Meta Cloud API for WhatsApp messaging.
'''
import os
import requests
from chatgpt_api import ChatGPTAPI
class WhatsAppAPI:
    def __init__(self, phone_number_id):
        '''
        Initializes the WhatsAppAPI with the provided API keys and phone number ID.
        Parameters:
        phone_number_id (str): The phone number ID for sending messages.
        '''
        self.api_key = os.getenv("WHATSAPP_API_KEY")
        self.chatgpt = ChatGPTAPI(os.getenv("CHATGPT_API_KEY"))
        self.phone_number_id = phone_number_id
        self.base_url = f"https://graph.facebook.com/v13.0/{self.phone_number_id}/messages"
    def send_message(self, recipient, message):
        '''
        Sends a message via WhatsApp API.
        Parameters:
        recipient (str): The recipient's phone number.
        message (str): The message text to send.
        '''
        headers = {
            "Authorization": f"Bearer {self.api_key}",
            "Content-Type": "application/json"
        }
        data = {
            "messaging_product": "whatsapp",
            "to": recipient,
            "text": {"body": message}
        }
        try:
            response = requests.post(self.base_url, headers=headers, json=data)
            response.raise_for_status()
            print(f"Message sent to {recipient}: {message}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Failed to send message: {e}")
    def receive_message(self, message):
        '''
        Handles incoming messages and generates a response using ChatGPT.
        Parameters:
        message (str): The incoming message text.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by ChatGPT.
        '''
        response = self.chatgpt.get_response(message)
        return response
```

chatgpt_api.py
```python
'''
Interfaces with the OpenAI ChatGPT API for intelligent conversation.
'''
import os
import openai
class ChatGPTAPI:
    def __init__(self, api_key):
        '''
        Initializes the ChatGPTAPI with the provided OpenAI API key.
        Parameters:
        api_key (str): The API key for authenticating with OpenAI.
        '''
        self.api_key = api_key
        openai.api_key = self.api_key
    def get_response(self, prompt):
        '''
        Gets a response from the ChatGPT model based on the provided prompt.
        Parameters:
        prompt (str): The input text to which the model should respond.
        Returns:
        str: The response generated by the ChatGPT model.
        '''
        try:
            response = openai.Completion.create(
                engine="text-davinci-003",
                prompt=prompt,
                max_tokens=150
            )
            return response.choices[0].text.strip()
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to get response from ChatGPT: {e}")
            return "Sorry, I'm having trouble understanding you right now."
```

database.py
```python
'''
Manages database operations for customer registration and booking.
'''
import sqlite3
class DatabaseManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.connection = sqlite3.connect('chatbot.db')
        self.create_tables()
    def create_tables(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS customers (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                name TEXT NOT NULL,
                phone TEXT NOT NULL
            )
        ''')
        cursor.execute('''
            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bookings (
                id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                customer_id INTEGER,
                service TEXT NOT NULL,
                date TEXT NOT NULL,
                FOREIGN KEY(customer_id) REFERENCES customers(id)
            )
        ''')
        self.connection.commit()
    def register_customer(self, customer_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO customers (name, phone) VALUES (?, ?)
        ''', (customer_data['name'], customer_data['phone']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def book_service(self, booking_data):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('''
            INSERT INTO bookings (customer_id, service, date) VALUES (?, ?, ?)
        ''', (booking_data['customer_id'], booking_data['service'], booking_data['date']))
        self.connection.commit()
    def get_bookings(self):
        cursor = self.connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM bookings')
        return cursor.fetchall()
```

notifications.py
```python
'''
Handles notification features for the application.
'''
import os
import smtplib
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
class NotificationManager:
    def __init__(self):
        self.smtp_server = os.getenv("SMTP_SERVER")
        self.smtp_port = os.getenv("SMTP_PORT")
        self.smtp_user = os.getenv("SMTP_USER")
        self.smtp_password = os.getenv("SMTP_PASSWORD")
    def send_notification(self, user_email, subject, message):
        '''
        Sends a notification to the specified user with the given message.
        Parameters:
        user_email (str): The recipient's email address.
        subject (str): The subject of the email.
        message (str): The message content of the email.
        '''
        try:
            # Set up the server
            server = smtplib.SMTP(self.smtp_server, self.smtp_port)
            server.starttls()
            server.login(self.smtp_user, self.smtp_password)
            # Create the email
            msg = MIMEMultipart()
            msg['From'] = self.smtp_user
            msg['To'] = user_email
            msg['Subject'] = subject
            msg.attach(MIMEText(message, 'plain'))
            # Send the email
            server.sendmail(self.smtp_user, user_email, msg.as_string())
            server.quit()
            print(f"Notification sent to {user_email}: {subject}")
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Failed to send notification: {e}")
```

'''
Handles deployment of the application on HOSTINGER.

import subprocess
class DeploymentManager:
    def __init__(self, hostinger_credentials):
        self.hostinger_credentials = hostinger_credentials
    def deploy_application(self):
        '''
        Deploys the application to HOSTINGER using the provided credentials.
        '''
        # Simulate deployment process
        print("Starting deployment to HOSTINGER...")
        # Example: Using subprocess to run deployment commands
        try:
            # This is a placeholder for actual deployment commands
            subprocess.run(["echo", "Deploying application..."], check=True)
            print("Application deployed successfully on HOSTINGER.")
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError as e:
            print(f"Deployment failed: {e}")
